Municipal Party Department to Examine the Academic Performance of Literacy School Students, Formulates Simple Rules for Examining the Academic Performance of Literacy Schools, Based on the Principle of Being Able to Recognize, Speak, and Write 97

The Literacy Education Association of the Municipal Party Department has established literacy schools in party departments and organizations at all levels, which will soon complete their studies. In order to examine the academic achievements of students in each school, it has specially formulated a "Simple Rules for Examining the Academic Performance of Private Literacy Schools," which is promulgated and implemented, and all cadres are notified to go to each school to conduct examinations according to the rules. The rules are recorded below: (Article 1) All academic examinations in literacy schools run by party departments and organizations at all levels, whether self-organized or acting as agents, shall be handled in accordance with these simple rules. (Article 2) After the literacy schools at all levels have completed their studies and held their own academic examinations, the teachers of the school shall prepare a list of qualified students and report it to the association five days in advance, and set a date and time to request the dispatch of personnel for spot checks. (Article 3) Each school shall conduct academic examinations in the following two types, and only those who pass both types shall be included in the list and submitted for spot checks. (Article 4) Those who can recognize but cannot speak, or those who can speak but cannot write, shall be supplemented by the teachers of each school until they can recognize, speak, and write. (Article 5) Spot checks shall be conducted by randomly selecting ten people from the list of qualified students reported by each school. The method is for each person to give a lesson and write a lesson. (Article 6) If the qualified students in each academic examination account for more than 80% of the number of people spot-checked, it shall be regarded as a complete graduation (limited to those on the submitted list). (Article 7) If the number of qualified students is less than 80% after the spot check, the spot check staff shall remove the unqualified students and randomly select several other people for examination until the ratio of 80% is reached. The unqualified students who have been removed shall be instructed to continue teaching by the teacher. (Article 8) Students who pass the spot check shall be given a certificate of academic achievement by the proctor on the spot. (Article 9) The test papers shall be taken back by the proctor and reported to the association for safekeeping. (Article 10) Each school shall issue a certificate of academic achievement to the students who pass the examination. (Article 11) These simple rules shall be submitted by the association to the Municipal Party Department and sent to the Education Bureau for record and implementation. (Article 12) These simple rules may be revised if there are any omissions.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Explains that Notifications Do Not Need to Affix Stamps Next Month, One Cent Stamp Still Required This Month 98

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday received a letter from the Knitwear Industry Association requesting an explanation regarding notifications. If no stamps are affixed, will it hinder the regulations? The association's reply is recorded below: Sir, we received your letter of the 6th stating that the notification is used to express the right to claim during the three festivals or at the end of the month. If no stamps are affixed, will it hinder the regulations? Please explain. After investigation, this notification, which has the effect of urging payment, is also called a reminder slip. The ministry has always stipulated that for amounts of one yuan or more, a one-cent stamp must be affixed. However, the Stamp Tax Law, which the National Government has scheduled to implement on September 1st, stipulates in Article 3, Paragraph 9 that account statements used to urge payment of debts or verify numbers are exempt from stamp duty. Therefore, the notification referred to by your association can be exempt from stamps starting from September 1st, but currently, it must still be stamped.

Party Departments on Both Railways Raise Relief Funds 99

The Special Party Departments of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways in this port believe that the floods in various provinces are extremely severe, the disaster area covers millions of square miles, and the disaster victims number over 30 million. They are displaced, and the sound of wailing can be heard everywhere, directly affecting the national economy and the people's livelihood. In view of this, the party department has launched a general mobilization of party members to donate to flood relief. The detailed methods are recorded below: (1) This method aims to provide relief to the floods in the Yellow River and Yangtze River basin provinces in 1935. (2) Relief funds are raised by the special party department organizing a donation team to be responsible for the management of various districts. (3) The organizational system of the fundraising team is as follows: 1. All executive and supervisory members and secretaries of the special party department are the general captains. 2. All executive and supervisory members of the district party departments are the district captains of each district. 3. All executive members of the district branch departments are the district branch captains of each district. (4) Party members and probationary party members of this railway are all members of the fundraising team. (5) All staff members of the special party department of this railway are all staff members of the fundraising team. (6) Each general captain must be responsible for raising at least 20 yuan in national currency. Each district captain and district branch captain must be responsible for raising at least 5 yuan in national currency. Each team member must be responsible for raising at least 2 yuan in national currency. Each staff member must be responsible for raising at least 10 yuan in national currency. (The above provisions are the minimum amounts. Those who can raise more donations and have excellent results will be rewarded separately by the executive committee of the special party department.) (7) The rewards for the fundraising team are based on the following two standards: 1. Based on the best fundraising results of each team. 2. Based on the best fundraising results of individuals. (8) Those who have already served as general captain or district captain and branch captain are no longer obligated to serve as team members to raise donations. (9) Those whose funds raised are less than the amount stipulated in Article 6 must still be supplemented by the member. (10) Donation receipts are printed and issued by the special party department. If there is insufficient supply, they may continue to be issued. (11) This donation work should be completed within one month. (12) After the fundraising period expires, all fundraising personnel shall submit the stubs of the donation receipts, together with the donations, level by level to the special party department for transfer to the central government for distribution. (13) After the donation is completed, the special party department shall publish the names and amounts of the donors in the Lianglu Weekly to show credibility. (14) When the staff members of the fundraising team go on business trips, it is a completely voluntary job and no public funds will be paid. (15) These methods shall be implemented by the executive committee of the special party department after approval.

The Sino-Foreign Charitable Relief Society Continues to Receive Recent Reports from Various Disaster Areas 101

Since receiving the bad news of the Yellow River and Yangtze River, the Sino-Foreign Charitable Relief Society on Renji Road has shocked Chinese and foreigners alike and is making every effort to raise relief funds. The telegrams and letters received from various disaster areas have been repeatedly recorded in previous reports. Now, the latest reports have been received and are recorded below:

Shandong. A letter from Wang Yide and other representatives of the disaster victims in Chengxian County stated that the amount of water in Chengxian this year is the largest in recent decades. When the official embankment breached this time, the waves rolled and poured straight into the abyss, heading east. In counties such as Dan, He, Ju, and Jia, where the flood arrived, only a vast expanse of water could be seen, with no villages to be found. The flooded area in the county, from the official embankment in the north to Shuncheng in the south, from Linpu in the west to Wuan in the east, is about 8,000 hectares. There are about 800 villages, and about -10,000 houses have collapsed. There are over 200,000 disaster victims, and over 2,000 people have drowned. The disaster victims who have not died are displaced everywhere. The washed-away grain and livestock are countless. The starving victims are awaiting food. In the midst of the scorching heat, the starving people who have been flooded will suffer from the plague again. Such suffering is even more unspeakable. I still appeal to you to quickly provide relief. Anhui. A telegram from Chen Dao and other representatives of the disaster victims in Guanzhuang, Tonglu County, stated, "Our village borders the Yangtze River and stretches for more than 60 miles, with 40,000 mu of fertile land and 60,000 residents. Since the disaster in Minguo, the vitality has been destroyed and has not yet recovered. Unexpectedly, the catastrophe has struck again. The northern embankment of the Yangtze River was reported to have collapsed on July 18. The fields, houses, and livestock were submerged, countless. The total loss in the village is about 2 million yuan. The disaster victims who failed to evacuate were buried in the bellies of fish. Those who were spared were also suffering from sleeping in the open and eating in the wind. Nine out of ten houses are empty, and there is no food to beg for. Moreover, after the drought, the autumn is approaching, and epidemics are prevalent. Hunger and cold are intertwined. It is expected that tens of thousands of disaster victims will fill the ditches sooner or later. Please allocate emergency relief to save the dying disaster victims." Anhui. A telegram from the Flood Relief and Work Relief Committee of Guangchengwei, Huaining County, stated, "Guangchengwei has been frequently flooded and drought-stricken, and the people's strength has been declining. The sores have not been healed, and another catastrophe has struck. The reason for the collapse is that there are no dams along the Yangtze River in the upstream Laohuchang area. The Yangtze River tides poured into the area, and the water suddenly rose several feet, resulting in deep suffering. As a result, tens of thousands of mu of planted land became the home of fish, and several thousand homes were turned into sacrifices. Displacement and migration are miserable and indescribable. The faces of the vegetable-eating victims are even more pitiful. It is now planned to repair the embankment and work instead of relief to save the disaster victims."

Refugees from Wenzhou Return Home on the Hai'an Steamer: Mayor Wu Generously Donates 100 Yuan in Relief Funds; Refugee Representatives Stay in Shanghai to Petition in Beijing Within Days 102

Seventy-four expelled overseas Chinese, including Hu Junmin, who were in Japan, faced financial difficulties and requested relief from the municipal government and reported their expulsion to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau. The authorities expressed deep sympathy for their plight. The Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau assigned personnel to distribute temporary relief funds of three yuan per person and a discounted round-trip steamer ticket from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. In addition, Mayor Wu generously donated 100 yuan in national currency for relief. Refugee representatives, including Hu Junmin, went to collect the funds yesterday morning and distributed them to the other refugees. According to Hu Junmin, who spoke to a reporter from the Industrial News Agency yesterday, they were deeply grateful for the assistance from the authorities, which prevented them from being stranded in Shanghai. They were also grateful for the generosity of the Jiangxi Guild Hall in providing accommodation, setting a good example for the world. To express their gratitude, they presented a large mirror frame as a memento. It is reported that the Wenzhou refugees boarded the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Hai'an steamer last night to return home, while others went to various places to seek a livelihood. However, a few refugee representatives are temporarily staying in Shanghai and plan to go to Beijing within days to report to various government agencies.

Five Exchanges Jointly Petition the Ministries of Finance and Industry to Ban Illegal Commercial Organizations that Disrupt Legitimate Business and Market Order; Request Approval to Ban Them According to Law to Maintain Government Authority 103

The Joint Association of Five Exchanges in Shanghai petitioned the central government because of the recent discovery of illegal commercial organizations similar to exchange trading that were affecting the reputation and business of the exchanges. A joint meeting was held on the 5th of this month to discuss countermeasures, and it was decided to petition the central authorities to strictly ban such organizations according to law in order to maintain business. Yesterday, the chairmen of the Cotton Cloth Exchange, Mu Ouchu; the Gold Exchange, Du Yuesheng; the Securities Exchange, Zhang Weiru; the Flour Exchange, Wang Yiting; and the Grain Exchange, Gu Xinyi, jointly petitioned the Ministries of Finance and Industry, requesting prompt approval to issue a general order to ban these organizations. The petition stated: "Regarding the petition to ban illegal commercial organizations similar to exchange trading and to protect legitimate business, it has been found that in recent times, a small number of unscrupulous individuals have taken advantage of extraterritoriality to establish illegal commercial organizations similar to exchange trading, openly buying and selling and profiting as intermediaries. The harm caused by this is unimaginable. These illegal organizations cater to the speculative psychology of those struggling financially, using small units to lure non-official merchants to entrust them with buying and selling. As a result, anyone with five, ten, or even two or three yuan can engage in buying and selling, ultimately being exploited by commissions and suffering disastrous losses due to market fluctuations. These illegal organizations have no fixed capital and are not subject to the regulations of the Exchange Law. If they encounter unfavorable circumstances, the clients who are involved have no legal protection. Countless people have been harmed by this and have no way to help themselves. At the same time, the business of legitimate exchanges is damaged, and the market is disrupted. Furthermore, in recent years, more and more Chinese people have engaged in trading in securities and goods on the American stock exchange, all handled by these illegal organizations. The capital lost and flowing out each year amounts to millions of yuan. This is not only alarming because of the huge outflow of cash, but also greatly reduces the liquidity of domestic securities and goods, leading to stagnation in the social economy. Article 16 of the Exchange Law clearly stipulates that no one may engage in the business of acting as an agent, introducing, or transmitting exchange transactions. If these illegal commercial organizations are allowed to exist, what is the point of national legislation? They should be strictly banned according to law, both to maintain the authority of our government and to protect the business of legitimate exchanges. This is in the public interest."

The representatives of the Shanghai industry and commerce petition, Zhang Ziguang, Shen Tianxin, Ma Jisheng, Lu Xingzhuang, Xu Jianruo, Yao Yizhang, Chen Zhibei, etc., returned to Shanghai from Nanjing at 11:30 the night before last. The representatives were satisfied and withdrew. The next day, they petitioned the Central Party Headquarters, where Secretary Yang Donglin received them, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, where Gu Zhenggang received them. Both promised to forward their intentions.

On the Ning Shao Steamer, a Young Man Leapt into the Sea: He Jumped into the Sea in the Outer Tongsha Waters, Leaving Behind a Letter, a Badge, and a Western Suit; His Name Was Zhu Qiming, Only Twenty-One Years Old 105

The Ning Shao Steamer Company's New Ning Shao steamer set sail from Shanghai for Ningbo at 5:00 pm on the 5th. A young passenger jumped into the sea when the ship passed the Tongsha waters. A reporter from the Datong News Agency has investigated and reported the details as follows:

Jumped into the Sea: The New Ning Shao steamer set sail from Shanghai for Ningbo at 5:00 pm on the 5th. At 8:00 pm that night, when the ship passed the Tongsha waters, a young passenger suddenly jumped into the sea from the upper bunk of a third-class cabin. The ship's purser, Li Ruiting, heard the alarm and ordered the ship to stop and search, but the currents were too strong, and he had already disappeared.

Letter Found: It was later discovered that the passenger was staying in the upper bunk of a third-class cabin. The cabin attendant, Zhong Rongtang, found a letter, a woolen suit, a badge, a small amount of foreign coins, and several picture books on his bunk. Nothing else was found and all were handed over to the purser's office.

Seemed Like an Athlete: The letter was addressed to his parents and written in pencil on作文 paper. It was sealed in blank foreign paper, but no address was written. The handwriting was elegant, and the wording was clear and fluent. The badge was about the size of a 20-cent silver coin, with the words "Cheng Yize Presented in 1932" engraved on one side and the words "China" engraved on the other. A flying eagle was engraved on the top, and a running figure was engraved on the bottom. Based on these items, the deceased was likely an athlete.

Contents of the Letter: Reading the letter, it was learned that the deceased's name was Zhu Qiming, and he was only twenty-one years old. He was a promising young man, so why did he do this? The cause of his death is truly speculative. The original text of his letter is as follows: "Dear Parents, I have a stubborn personality and have lived for twenty-one years. I will never forget the care and nurturing you have given me. However, on this autumn night, I must bid you farewell forever. Alas, this gray universe hides emptiness and indifference. When the fierce winds and rainstorms attack my weak will, I have tasted enough pain from repeated encounters. Fate is mocking me, and I feel that life is dull. I will eventually follow the aimless pursuit, filled with the terror of existence. Let me stop breathing as soon as possible, and I will be content. Alas, the end of my life will be tonight under the autumn moon. Farewell, my flesh and blood parents, and everything in the world. Your unfilial son, Zhu Qiming, written August 5th."

Final Words: At the end of the letter were the following words, with a sad and poignant tone, thought to be his last words before death: "All grievances will be repaid in the next life. Do not grieve for my unfilial death." The ship returned to Shanghai yesterday, and the items were handed over to the Jiangxi Road General Bureau by the ship's purser, Li Ruiting, for the family to claim.

Wu Song Merchants Oppose the Bureau of Finance's Increased Assessment of Rent 106

The Municipal Bureau of Finance recently sent tax collectors and inspectors to the Wu Song district to investigate the rent of various shops and increase the assessed rent to increase property tax revenue. For example, the monthly rent of Wan Sheng Sauce Garden was originally 70 yuan, but it is now assessed at 120 yuan. The rent of Shun Tai Yuan Silk Shop was originally 40 yuan, but it is now assessed at 65 yuan. Other shops, such as Hu Xiang Xing and Xu Hong Sheng, have also had their rents increased by one-half or one-third. After hearing the news, the shops expressed their opposition, saying that Wu Song had only recently recovered from the war and that now was a time of economic downturn and hardship for the people. They could not afford to have their rent increased. They sent letters to the Wu Song Chamber of Commerce, urging them to forward their concerns to the Bureau of Finance and maintain the old assessed rent to ease the merchants' difficulties.

Manager of Tong Qing Money Exchange and Others Accused of Embezzlement; Case Resolved; Police Agree to Withdraw Charges; Xia Guichu Posts Reliable Shop Guarantee 107

Xia Guichu, a Ningbo native and manager of the Tong Qing Money Exchange at 180 Ningbo Road, and Zhu Haichu, a Huzhou native and assistant manager, were recently accused by shareholders Xu Maotang and others, through lawyer E Sen, to the General Police Station of colluding in embezzlement and misappropriating public funds amounting to 524,393.23 yuan. Chinese detective Chen Yaoting and Western detective Warren G. S. arrested Xia and Zhu and charged them with embezzlement in the First Special District Court. After one hearing, the court ordered a postponement. Xia Guichu was returned to custody, and Zhu Haichu was allowed to post 100,000 yuan in cash or a shop guarantee. This was reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide of the First Special District Court opened the criminal court for a continued hearing. The plaintiffs first presented sufficient evidence, but because the plaintiffs and defendants had now reached a settlement, the evidence was not presented, making it impossible for the police to conduct an investigation. According to the plaintiffs, they wanted the police to withdraw the public prosecution in the case. The Western detective in charge consulted the district chief, who stated that according to Article 248 of the Criminal Procedure Law, a public prosecution could be withdrawn before the conclusion of the first instance debate. Therefore, he agreed to the plaintiff's request, but the article stipulated that the withdrawal must be in writing. Therefore, he requested the court to postpone the case for a week so that a written request could be submitted within that time to withdraw the charges. Xia Guichu's lawyers, Fan Gang and Zhao Fuding, argued that since the police had requested a withdrawal, Xia should be allowed to post a guarantee to appear when summoned. Zhu Haichu's lawyer, Wu Linkun, said that according to police precedent, withdrawals were not made in writing. Since the police lawyer had verbally stated that he was withdrawing the charges, the court should consider the charges withdrawn to avoid delaying the proceedings. Judge Feng stated that the new Criminal Law stipulated that withdrawals must be made in writing. Police prosecutions were usually made with a case report, so at a minimum, a case report requesting a withdrawal should be submitted. Therefore, he ordered the case to be postponed for one week, and Xia Guichu was allowed to post a reliable shop guarantee for release.

Sun Cailing's Young Son Kidnapped; Ransom of 500,000 Yuan Demanded; Police Requested to Rescue; Chinese and Western Detectives Investigating 108

The newly built three-story Western-style house at 50, Lane 344, Beile Road, in the French Concession, is owned by Sun Cailing, a native of Ningbo. Sun is currently an employee of the China Farmers Bank in Hankou. He has a wife and four sons. Except for the eldest son, who suffers from mental illness, the other three sons are studying at a nearby school. On the afternoon of the 5th, Sun's youngest son, who is nine years old, was playing in the lane and suddenly disappeared. Sun's wife discovered this and ordered the male and female servants to search everywhere, but they could not be found. While Sun and others were anxious, the kidnappers sent someone to throw a letter through the glass window of the back door. The letter demanded a ransom of 500,000 yuan. Sun Cailing and others were shocked after reading the letter and realized that the boy had been kidnapped. They reported the information to the French police in charge of the area and requested that they send officers to investigate the kidnappers and rescue the boy. After receiving the report, the police chief dispatched a large number of Chinese and Western detectives to investigate.

Huang Xianyao's Forgery Case Continued; Huang's Lawyer Presented a Letter Proving Huang Was Deceived 109

Huang Xianyao, the son of the late Huang Chujiu, founder of the Gong Fa Company's Day and Night Bank and the Great World, previously hired lawyer Mi Jingshen to file a case seeking to live with his wife, Zhou. Mi and his clerk, Wu Jiajin, forged a document stating that 100,000 yuan of property was deposited with his father-in-law, Zhou Songqing, and petitioned the Shanghai District Court for mediation, hoping to defraud his father-in-law of money. Later, because the mediation failed, Wang Shaozeng, a creditor of the Gong Fa Company, obtained the forged document and hired lawyer Xu Yannian to file a complaint with the Second Special District Court Criminal Division, accusing Zhou Songqing and his son-in-law Huang Xianyao of damaging creditors' rights. Because Huang failed to appear in court, the court arrested Huang. The court then opened a safety deposit box at the Guohua Bank and retrieved the forged document. Zhou Songqing reported the matter to the police, accusing Huang Xianyao, Mi Jingshen, Wu Jiajin, and others of forging documents. After police investigation and identification, the document was confirmed to be a forgery and not written by Zhou. Because the two defendants, Mi and Wu, had already left Shanghai, Huang Xianyao was handed over to the Second Special District Court, and the police department lawyer filed a public prosecution under Article 210 of the Criminal Law for forgery. Judge Li Changnian questioned Huang and ordered him to be detained pending a further hearing with the other defendants. This was reported in detail in the 30th of last month. At 11:00 am yesterday, Judge Li of the Second Special District Court continued the hearing in the First Criminal Division. Fei Xizhen represented the police department in court. The detective in charge of the case, Lu Zhixiang, reported that the two defendants, Mi Jingshen and Wu Jiajin, had fled and could not be summoned to court. The plaintiff, Zhou Songqing, 73 years old, testified that Huang Xianyao was his son-in-law. After he requested mediation in the District Court in September of the 22nd year, he was originally going to sue him, but his mother spoke for him, saying that he was mentally ill, and his daughter pleaded with him, so he dropped the matter. He did not know about the document until he was accused and Judge Shu showed him a photo of the document. He then learned that it was forged and that there was no such thing. Wang Shaozeng filed the accusation on December 28th of last year. The defendant Huang Xianyao, 31 years old, from Yuyao, testified that he worked in a Chinese and Western pharmacy. An officer gave Huang a pencil draft to look at and asked, "Did you write this paper?" Huang replied, "Yes, this is the draft. According to your statement, this document was not written by your father-in-law, is that right?" Huang replied, "Yes, it was made by Wu Jiajin at Mi Jingshen's place. I originally hired a lawyer to handle the cohabitation case, and he did this. I didn't see who wrote this document, and I didn't receive this document. It was given to Mi by Wu. Tang Shouchun was present at the time. Tang tried to extort money but failed and gave the photograph to the creditor. I didn't go to the mediation court at first. Later, Tang told me to say that this document was found in my wife's clothing box." At this point, Huang's defense lawyer presented a letter from Wu Jiajin to Huang and a photograph of Wu, stating that the letter was found by Huang's family at home, which proved that Huang had been deceived. Huang said that he received the letter two or three months after the previous mediation because he did not trust Wu. He sent the letter as a guarantee. The court examined the letter and filed the photograph, returning the letter to the defendant's defense lawyer. The court then stated that the facts of the case still needed to be studied in detail, and the files of the previous case needed to be reviewed for reference. The hearing was postponed to the 16th, and the defendant was returned to custody. The court also told the plaintiff, Zhou Songqing, to submit any evidence in the case as soon as possible. If there were witnesses, they should be brought to court for questioning next time. The court then adjourned.

Superstitious Belief in Divine Power; A Girl's Life Wrongfully Lost; Ji Gong's Ineffectiveness, Incense Ashes Useless; Shen Shoutang and Others Sued in Court 110

Shen Shoutang, a carpenter from Zhejiang, and Xiang Xueshu, from Jiading, usually believed in Buddhism, so they gathered ten comrades to rent a house at 81 Hanbilili Road, Hongkou, to set up Ji Gong Hall, specializing in using divine blessings to cure children's illnesses. On the morning of the 14th of last month, Wang Ming, a native of Yangzhou living at 18 Ruikangli, Jiaxing Road, because his seven-year-old granddaughter, A-San, suddenly fell ill, heard that Ji Gong Hall had a divine spirit to cure diseases, so Wang Ming's daughter-in-law, Wang Jiangshi, took A-San to seek treatment. Shen and others charged ten yuan. After paying a deposit of one yuan, Shen and others gave them a talisman, totaling twelve, and several packets of incense ashes, instructing them to mix them with boiling water and drink them at home. On the 18th, they went for another consultation and paid another half yuan. Shen and others still used the previous method, instructing them to ingest the ashes. Unexpectedly, after taking them, A-San's condition worsened the next day and she soon died. Wang believed that his granddaughter's death was caused by Shen and others, so he hired lawyer Huang Xiubo to file a lawsuit against Shen and Xiang in the First Special District Court for the crime of using sorcery to confuse people and causing death through negligence. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui presided over the hearing in the Eighth Criminal Division. The two defendants also surrendered with their defense lawyers. The plaintiff, Wang Ming, and his daughter-in-law, Wang Jiangshi, also surrendered, stating that when they went to seek treatment, Xiang Xueshu acted as Ji Gong, treating the illness at a table, and Shen gave them talismans and incense ashes, and A-San's condition worsened after taking them, and she died on the 19th. They had paid 1.5 yuan and requested an investigation. The two defendants stated that the plaintiff came on their own accord to seek a divination from the Ji Gong spirit, so they gave them talismans and incense ashes, telling them to swallow them with boiling water, and denied receiving any money. After the lawyers for both sides debated, Judge Liu declared the debate closed and ordered the two defendants to each provide a shop guarantee for appearance when summoned, pending sentencing on the morning of the 9th.

Three Men Jumped into the Huangpu River; All Due to Economic Pressure; Fortunately, They Were Rescued Separately; Did Not Suffer a Drowning Death 111

On the night before last and yesterday, three men jumped into the Huangpu River, all due to economic pressure. Fortunately, they were rescued separately and sent to charitable organizations for relief. The details are as follows:

Wu Xikang, 33 years old, from Huai'an, was struggling financially. At around 6:00 pm the night before last, he hired a sampan numbered 315 at the Chunjiang Wharf in Pudong, saying that he wanted to cross to the Muddy Bank in South Shanghai and agreed to pay 20 cents for the fare. However, when the boat reached the waters near Cheqi Port, Wu suddenly paid one yuan and then jumped off to commit suicide. He was rescued by the boatman and sent to the Customs Water Police Station, and then to a charitable organization for relief.

Zhong Weixin, 30 years old, from Ningbo, had been unemployed for a long time and had no home to return to, so he became despondent. At 10:00 am yesterday, he jumped into the Huangpu River from the Baidu Bridge outside the Suzhou Creek. He was rescued by the police and taken to the Customs Water Police Station, and then to the Ningbo Association for relief.

Shen Yongjin, 28 years old, from Ningbo, had borrowed money to purchase soda to sell, but he was struggling financially due to the small profit. At 8:15 am yesterday, he boarded a Taikoo Company express ferry at the Yangjingbang Wharf. When the ship reached the middle of the river, Shen jumped into the Huangpu River to commit suicide. He was rescued by the boatman and sent to the Customs Water Police Station, and then to the Ningbo Association for relief.

Wu Xikang Fell and Drowned 113

Wu Xikang, 33 years old, from Huaicheng, who lived at 40 Changleli, Hengfeng Road, Zhabei, usually made a living by collecting leftover food (commonly known as "leftovers") from various restaurants. At around 8:00 pm the night before last, he was cooling off on the Hengfeng Road Bridge when he fell into the river. By the time he was pulled out, he was already dead. Yesterday morning, the local police station ordered the local security chief, Li Ruiru, to report the case to the court for inspection. Later, the deceased's father, Wu Shenzheng, petitioned the court to waive the inspection, stating, "The deceased had four sons. The eldest son, Xikang, carelessly fell into the river and drowned. It was no one's fault. I request a waiver of the inspection and am willing to arrange for the coffin and burial," and so on. After being questioned by prosecutor Tang Ruxiu, the request was granted, and he was instructed to arrange for the coffin and burial as soon as possible.

Reasons Why Telephone Prices Should Not Be Increased in the Extraterritorial Road Area: Telephone Rates in the Extraterritorial Area Are Already High; Furthermore, the Telephones Used Have Not Been Converted to Automatic 114

The Shanghai Telephone Company's telephone price increase is due to the construction of extraterritorial roads in both Huxi and Hubei. Because the sovereignty belongs to the Shanghai Municipal Government, the Municipal Public Utility Bureau has sent a letter to the company, stating that if the company wants to increase the price of telephones installed in the area, it must first obtain permission from the Municipal Government. Otherwise, telephone users in the area will not be charged the increased price. The details have been reported in various newspapers. Yesterday, a reporter inquired with someone familiar with the matter. According to them, the sovereignty of the extraterritorial road area belongs to the Shanghai Municipal Government, and the telephone price increase should first be approved by the Municipal Government. Furthermore, the Shanghai Telephone Company's price list stipulates that telephone prices outside the concession must be agreed upon with the administrative head other than the authorities of the Public Concession and the French Concession before they can take effect. Moreover, telephone prices in the extraterritorial road area are one or two yuan higher per phone than in the two concessions. Telephone charges in the extraterritorial road area in Hubei are particularly high and should not be increased again. In addition, the contract between the company and the two concession authorities stipulates that prices can only be increased after all telephones have been converted to automatic. Currently, telephones in the extraterritorial road area in Huxi have not been converted to automatic, but prices are being increased at the same time as in the concession, which is inappropriate. Therefore, the Public Utility Bureau's prevention of the telephone company's price increase in the extraterritorial road area is not only a matter of sovereignty but also for the benefit of telephone users and is therefore supported by the citizens.

The Determination of the Domestic Cigarette Industry: Today is the 88 National Cigarette Day, with the Slogan "Chinese People Should Smoke Chinese Cigarettes." The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Holds a Grand Meeting, and Major Newspapers Publish Special Editions 115

The China National Cigarette Maintenance Association, from its initiation and preparation to its establishment, has gone through the unanimous efforts of representatives from both the cigarette factories and the color printing industries. It has also received enthusiastic cooperation from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Industrial and Commercial Renaissance Association, the media, and various leaders. Its reputation has spread, causing a national sensation, and its business prospects are showing a thriving outlook. It has now been resolved by the Standing Committee that August 8th (today) will be designated as the 88 National Cigarette Day, as a commemoration of cooperative unity, coexistence, and shared prosperity, and as an expression of nationwide mobilization for expanded promotion. The association has also officially designated "Chinese people should smoke Chinese cigarettes" as the unified external slogan. The current status of the association's commemorative day activities will be recorded below:

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Holds a Grand Commemorative Meeting: Today at 2:30 PM, the association will hold a commemorative meeting in the Standing Committee Room of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to celebrate the establishment of the 88 National Cigarette Day. Representatives from various cigarette factories will attend the meeting. The standing committee members of the association, including Yuan Ludeng, Shen Weiting, Shen Xingde, Lao Jingxiu, Jing Yimeng, Ding Houqing, Bao Gengsheng, Wu Linzhe, Sun Daosheng, Ding Zhenbo, Shen Wen, and others, will all be present to host the event. Representatives from political, academic, business, and journalistic circles, as well as leaders from various industries, have also been invited to attend and provide guidance, with the aim of concentrating efforts and vigorously promoting domestic products.

Major Newspapers in the City Publish Special Editions: Since the establishment of the association, the media has unanimously supported it. Today, in commemoration of the 88 Day, special editions are being published in major newspapers, each being a special edition for the 88 National Cigarette Day. The writers are all reporters from major newspapers. The "Xinwen Bao" features Yan Duhe, Yu Kongwo, and Jiang Jianhou; "Shen Bao" features Wu Tingchen, Qu Shao Yi, Zhao Junhao, Zhou Shoujuan, Ma Chonggan, Pan Yangrao, Huang Jiping, and Sun Daosheng; "Chen Bao" features Si Xia, Hu Tisheng, Xu Zhuodai, Wang Qixu, and Wu Han; "Shishi Xinbao" features Huang Tianpeng and Nie Shiqi; "Shibao" features Teng Shuke; "Minbao" features Guan Jiu'an, Wu Zhongyi, and Jiang Hongjiao; "Shanghai Shangbao" features Lu Sihong and others, all demonstrating brilliant writing and creating unique styles, which will surely be loved by readers nationwide. The promotional effect will be unparalleled.

Grand Comic Variety Show on the Air: Today, the association will host a grand comic variety show at the Wireless Radio Research Society of the Great World Entertainment Center, from 6:45 PM to 10:30 PM. Famous comic performers have been invited to broadcast comic skits. Furthermore, Yuan Ludeng and Shen Weiting, members of the Standing Committee of the association, will deliver speeches on the radio. At the same time, all radio stations in the city will uniformly promote the association's slogan, "Chinese people should smoke Chinese cigarettes." The comic program schedule is as follows: 6:45 PM to 7:15 PM, Zhao Xixi and Haoyundao; 7:15 PM to 8:00 PM, Liu Chunshan and Sheng Daidai; 8:15 PM to 9:00 PM, Lu Xixi and Lu Qiqi; 9:00 PM to 9:30 PM, Jiang Xiaoxiao and Bao Lele; 9:30 PM to 10:30 PM, Pei Yanghua, Cheng Xiaoting, Fan Haha, and Guan Wuling.

Chinese Cinemas Screen Slides: In order to arouse the Shanghai moviegoers to buy and smoke domestic cigarettes, Wu Linzhe, a member of the Standing Committee of the association, specially requested Zhou Jianyun and Bian Yuying of the Huawei Trading Company to contact major Chinese cinemas. Starting today, before and after the film screenings, a slide with the message "Chinese people should smoke Chinese cigarettes" will be inserted. This is entirely voluntary. More than ten cinemas have agreed, including Jincheng, Central, Mingxing, Southeast, Dong, Xin Central, Xihai, Rongjin, Huade, Penglai, Kade, and Wanguo.

Oil Piandee is Involved in a Lawsuit with the Continental Bank: The First Special Court Continued the Hearing Yesterday Morning. The Guanghua Company Entrusted a Lawyer to Participate in the Litigation. The Continental Bank Requested the Court to Reject the Lawsuit Based on Legal Principles. 118

The case between the Soviet Russian Oil Piandee Oil Trust Company and the Guanghua Oil Company, with the Continental Bank as the guarantor of the debt, was heard for the second instance in the First Special District Court at 9:30 AM yesterday. Judge Li Hu presided over the hearing. The plaintiff was still represented by foreign attorney Wei Lv, and the defendant, the Continental Bank, was represented by attorney Xu Shihao. The Guanghua Company was represented by attorney Wang Xiaowen. Both parties made their arguments, which lasted for two and a half hours. The plaintiff first made a supplementary statement of reasons for filing the lawsuit. Then, defendant Xu Shihao stood up and made his defense. The two most important points were that the Continental Bank was the guarantor of Guanghua's debt, and that it seemed inappropriate for Oil Piandee to directly sue the Continental Bank without first dealing with Guanghua. Secondly, regarding Guanghua's debt to Oil Piandee, the defendant had forwarded the plaintiff's letter to Guanghua, and the reply stated that they absolutely could not pay on their behalf. Therefore, although the defendant wanted to pay Oil Piandee, it was impossible, because if the payment was not recognized by Guanghua in the future, who would the defendant seek debt from? Finally, Wang Xiaowen, the attorney representing Guanghua, also stood up and requested that the lawsuit be suspended, because there were still other procedural entanglements between Guanghua and Oil Piandee that needed to be resolved legally. In the end, the court adjourned and the plaintiff, defendant, and participant left the courtroom to await the court's decision on a scheduled date. The Continental Bank's statement of defense is recorded as follows: "Statement of defense regarding the case of the Oil Piandee Company suing for guaranteed debt. Regarding the contract signed by the plaintiff and Guanghua Oil Company on November 1st last year for the sale of kerosene, the Guanghua Company and the plaintiff first requested the defendant to sign a guarantee. At that time, the defendant and its agent, attorney Xu Shihao, considered that the content of the guarantee established by the plaintiff was inappropriate and the scope was too broad. Moreover, regarding the amount, the original guarantee stated US$400,000, but the defendant only acknowledged guaranteeing half of that amount. Furthermore, Chapter 6 of the guarantee stated, 'Our bank allows for the immediate payment to your company of any of the aforementioned funds when Guanghua Oil Company fails to fulfill the obligations of the aforementioned contracts, or any of the aforementioned contracts, and our bank has no conditions,' which clearly placed the guarantor in the same position as the principal debtor, Guanghua Company. This greatly deviated from the principles of guaranteed debt, and completely eliminated the guarantor's rights of prior recourse and search for assets, which was greatly different from the defendant's original intention to act as a guarantor. After repeated negotiations, and stating that it would not sign the agreement without changes to the guarantee, the plaintiff agreed to change the scope and responsibility of the guarantee, and stated that the guarantee and contract documents had been sent to the Moscow headquarters. However, for the sake of convenience, both parties could exchange letters to clarify the basis for the amendment. The defendant and the plaintiff then exchanged letters simultaneously, and Article 6 stated, 'If Guanghua fails to fulfill part or all of the obligations in the aforementioned guarantee, your company should first give our bank two weeks' written notice, and at the same time, before requesting payment from our bank, should first make every effort to have Guanghua pay the funds. Your company should also present all evidence on which the request for payment from Guanghua is based when requesting payment from our bank,' etc. Therefore, according to the content of the exchanged letters, even if the plaintiff believed that Guanghua Company had failed to fulfill any of the terms of the original contract, it could only file a lawsuit against Guanghua Company based on Article 6 of the exchanged letters and fully assert its claims. (The phrase in the exchanged letters, 'make every effort to have Guanghua pay the funds,' includes the procedure of filing a lawsuit, which is very clear.) Given that the defendant was originally in the position of guarantor, its inherent rights of prior recourse and search for assets were not waived at all. How could the plaintiff directly file a lawsuit against the defendant alone, thereby violating the litigation procedures? Furthermore, Guanghua Company has already filed a statement to participate in the lawsuit, and based on Article 14 of the original contract, if there is an event of force majeure, the contract should be temporarily suspended, and neither party shall bear any losses. In terms of the facts, since December of last year, the domestic market situation has been unprecedentedly depressed for decades, and the kerosene business has also been affected, as has been the case for all companies, not just Guanghua. This serious change was an unforeseen fact and an uncontrollable phenomenon. According to the provisions of Article 14 on force majeure in the contract, Guanghua Company has absolutely no liability for compensation. Therefore, the defendant, based on the relationship of guaranteed debt, has no further responsibility. Even if we take a step back and disregard Article 14 of the contract, and assume that the principal debtor, Guanghua Company, cannot be exempted from liability, it is essential that the plaintiff first sue Guanghua Company to pursue execution from the standpoint of the defendant's right to search for assets. If its property is insufficient for repayment, then it can make a claim against the defendant. Before suing Guanghua Company, the plaintiff has absolutely no reason to file a lawsuit against the defendant alone and ignore Guanghua, both legally and factually. Therefore, this statement of defense is filed, and it is humbly requested that your court review it promptly and issue a judgment rejecting the plaintiff's lawsuit and ordering it to bear the litigation costs. This would be greatly appreciated."

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Sends a Letter to the Arts and Crafts Bureau, Requesting that It Not Impose Excessive Fines on Bicycles. Convey to the Police Department Not to Impose Further Fines on Bicycles Traveling Without Violating Regulations 119

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Public Concession Engineering Bureau yesterday, stating, "Regarding the letter from the Bicycle Repair Industry Association of the city on the 6th of this month, reporting that various bicycle shops in the central district have been reporting that in recent months, the British police have been driving prison vans from 9 PM every night, regardless of the circumstances, detaining large numbers of bicycles along the road, sending them to the police station, and sentencing them to fines before returning the vehicles. As a result, passengers dare not inquire, and businesses are on the verge of collapse. The members of the association have opened bicycle shops, donated registration certificates in accordance with regulations, and paid various taxes, so why should they be harassed and hinder commerce for no reason? Moreover, at a time when all industries are declining, the bicycle shop industry relies on the income of the summer and autumn seasons to make up for the losses in the remaining winter. Now, they are being suppressed by the police. If this continues until winter, they will inevitably be unable to maintain their livelihoods. Thinking of this, they cannot help but feel chilled to the bone. We should request your association to seriously negotiate to maintain the members' last hope of survival.

Based on this, the association found that the British police were obstructing vehicles, and after receiving reports from the same industry, the reason for the detention was unknown. If this continues, our fellow traders will inevitably suffer a great impact. We are specifically reporting the true situation and requesting your association to promptly negotiate and correct the British police's abuse of detaining bicycles in order to provide relief and stabilize commerce. Based on this, the association found that bicycle shops established in the public concession area have donated registration certificates in accordance with regulations and paid various taxes. Therefore, there is no violation of regulations in renting out the vehicles, and excessive fines should absolutely not be imposed. According to the aforementioned situation, the industry is being pushed to the brink of collapse. We are hereby sending a letter, hoping that your bureau will operate and promptly convey to the police department that bicycles traveling within the concession that do not violate the regulations should no longer be detained in order to maintain business. We would be deeply grateful."

August 8th National Goods Cigarette Festival Special Edition 140

Thoughts on Revitalizing the Cigarette Industry 141

— Shen Bao, Wu Tingchen

I was born late. In the short span of several decades, material changes have been numerous. The last twenty years have been especially significant. Taking cigarettes as an example, I cannot help but feel a sense of vicissitude. Tobacco flowed into China no more than three hundred years ago. When I was young, I often saw farmers in the fields with an old bamboo root pipe in hand. They would drill a hole next to the root, fill it with tobacco, strike a flint, and a wisp of clear smoke would rise. They would use it to relax during breaks from work. As for the gentry, officials, and women in their chambers, the pipes they used were either made of copper or silver, with tassels hanging from the top and embroidered pouches attached to the bottom, making them even more luxurious. As a result, dry and water tobacco shops were set up everywhere in the city. This was the era when native tobacco was popular. Forty years ago, imported cigarettes flowed in continuously. Later, foreign merchants even established factories in China to manufacture them. At that time, smokers were merely driven by curiosity, holding a cigarette in their mouths simply to show off their fashion. Later, due to their convenience of carrying and simple smoking method, they became more and more popular. The outflow of money caused commentators to believe that it was no less than opium. Socially conscious people even established non-cigarette smoking associations, but the trend could not be stopped. This was the era when foreign cigarettes sold well. Chinese entrepreneurs saw that imported cigarettes were selling like hotcakes and that there must be great profits to be made. They then set up factories to imitate them. Nanyang started first, and Huacheng followed. After the May Thirtieth Movement, small and medium-sized factories sprung up like mushrooms after rain. The strength of Chinese cigarettes not only filled the domestic market but could also be exported abroad. Wherever the footsteps of overseas Chinese reached, national cigarettes followed. This was the golden age of national cigarettes. Seeing the rise of the Chinese cigarette industry, foreign merchants, fearing that it might hinder their business, relied on their strong capital and used their diplomatic skills. In an instant, the Chinese factories gradually showed signs of being unable to sustain themselves. In the past two years, they had also engaged in behind-the-scenes struggles, opening up new fronts and attempting to struggle, but ultimately it did not help to alleviate their decline, which is truly regrettable.

Some say that China is a country founded on agriculture, but the raw materials for food and clothing are largely imported. According to the Bank of China's report for the twenty-third year of the Republic (1934), the import of agricultural products that year reached more than 334 million yuan. Among them, rice accounted for more than 65.6 million yuan, cotton accounted for more than 90 million yuan, and wheat accounted for more than 31.8 million yuan. Why do you alone loudly advocate for the cigarette industry, which is unrelated to people's livelihood? Is this not inappropriate? I say that the items listed above are the result of natural and man-made disasters. Once the countryside recovers, it is hoped that the imports may decrease. However, the decline of the cigarette industry is aimed at foreign merchants. Therefore, without conducting research on production and sales, it is impossible to hope for its revitalization. Nor can it be effective by the efforts of manufacturers alone. It must be through the joint assistance of the Chinese people that it can be remedied. It must be known that although cigarettes are a consumable item, there are many people who grow tobacco, many who make cigarettes, many who sell cigarettes, and many others who are indirectly engaged in the cigarette industry. One industry, however small, is related to such a large number of people. Chinese people who smoke cigarettes should, when they have one in their mouths, silently think about whether it was grown by Chinese people and made by Chinese people. If it is a national cigarette, they should then put it in their mouths. Then, the national cigarette manufacturers will directly benefit, and the tobacco farmers and tobacco workers can also maintain their livelihoods. As for the manufacturers themselves, they should work hard day and night to constantly improve. This goes without saying.

Confession of an Old Brand Smoker 142

— Xinwen Bao, Yu Kongwo

I, this old brand smoker, was a person who didn't smoke cigarettes five years ago. Two or three cigarettes would dry my throat. But no one would have thought that now I smoke an average of seventy cigarettes a day. When talking to familiar friends about the number of cigarettes they smoke, I haven't encountered an opponent. No one has exceeded my record.

On average, each cigarette takes eight minutes to consume. In one hour, I can only smoke seven or eight cigarettes. Generally speaking, I spend eight or nine hours a day surrounded by misty smoke. To a high degree, I don't like to use a lighter. I pass the flame from one cigarette to the next. Friends can believe this. When they meet me, they always see me with a cigarette in my mouth. Cartoonists might think that this cigarette is more important than any part of my eyes, nose, or any other part of my face.

Here, I want to talk about how my cigarette consumption has increased so dramatically. Even I myself am puzzled. Perhaps the bitterness of life is the biggest reason people smoke. It's a pity I never understood elegant words such as stimulating thoughts and increasing inspiration.

There are probably more than just me who smoke because of the bitterness of life. Therefore, talking about quitting cigarettes is simply asking me to be suffocated to death. However, based on my experience as an "old brand smoker," I feel that many people "superstitiously" believe that imported cigarettes are better because of their expensive price. I am fundamentally opposed from head to toe. My reason is that cigarettes are a daily necessity, like rice. You can't compare the taste of eating them with the mindset of eating bird's nest or shark fin. In such an economic downturn, "rice" is impossible not to eat. If it were unnecessary luxuries like shark fin or bird's nest, you could simply not smoke them.

Therefore, from the standpoint of an "old brand smoker," I would like to advise my fellow smokers: If you don't need to smoke, it is best not to smoke. If you have to smoke them as a substitute for tea and food like I do, you should still smoke national cigarettes. Of course, advocating national goods is a national duty. At the same time, I feel that eating "rice" must be eating foreign "rice." You are simply a bit "foreign" or, you could say, "slavish"…

Promoting National Cigarettes 143

— Chen Bao, He Xiya

Cigarettes can invigorate the mind and aid in writing, so those engaged in a life of writing often enjoy them. And I enjoy them even more. Since I enjoy them, I cannot help but have my own preferences. This is why I am happy to talk about the benefits of this thing today.

Smoking cigarettes can also avoid filth, resolve fishy smells, dispel worries, eliminate depression, enjoy guests, and aid in conversation. Its use is so broad that it is no less than a necessity. When traveling alone in a hotel and bored, whenever the wine is drunk, the songs are sung, after meals and tea, light a cigarette, savor the taste endlessly, and the fragrance fills the air, and the whole body is soothed. It is not only for scholars to monopolize, but also for everyone to enjoy.

From the perspective of our country's national economy today, the act of smoking cigarettes should not be promoted. However, precisely because it is an economic issue, national cigarettes have a bitter reason that makes it impossible not to promote them. One is to reduce the outflow of wealth, and the other is to maintain the livelihoods of tobacco farmers and cigarette workers. It is only out of necessity.

Today's China is an extremely serious transitional era. Because of this, general phenomena in society are all filled with contradictory postures. The promotion and prohibition of cigarette smoking are also one of its ends. However, we believe that if we can base this on the spirit of loving the country and promoting national goods, we should examine this opportunity. What should be preserved? What should be promoted? This is understood by everyone and does not require further discussion. As for cigarettes, we can come to a conclusion: It is better to boldly promote smoking national cigarettes than to smoke foreign cigarettes.

August 8th National Goods Cigarette Festival Declaration 144

Our association announces its establishment, just twenty days ago. In order to expand publicity and make it lasting, we have designated August 8th as the National Goods Cigarette Festival and published this special edition to strengthen our support. We, the committee members, are tasked with a heavy responsibility. On this auspicious occasion, we cannot remain silent. We would like to say a few words to our fellow countrymen.

Since the opening of the sea borders, goods from the East and West have been flowing into China in increasing quantities. Cigarettes have also been sold in our country along with this commercial war. Later, foreign merchants set up cigarette factories in Shanghai, Hankou, Tianjin, and other places, manufacturing and selling them in large quantities. The business rights for cigarette sales in our country were entirely controlled by them. By the late Qing Dynasty, the Chinese people began to pay attention to this. They raised funds to set up cigarette factories, but due to poor management and crude equipment, they all failed. However, they continued to try one after another, never losing heart. Since the May Thirtieth Movement, more and more Chinese have invested in cigarette factories. The business of Chinese factories has flourished, recovering profits and rights to no small extent. However, the capital of Chinese factories is mostly weak, and the scale and equipment are also simple and crude. Even with all their efforts, they cannot compete with foreign factories. Therefore, the proportion of business between the two sides still has the momentum of the guest dominating the host. In recent years, tax rates have repeatedly increased, making the burden even heavier. They are externally pressured by the fierce competition of foreign cigarettes and internally troubled by the encirclement of smuggled cigarettes. Chinese factories are in a difficult situation, struggling to cope. Many of those that have difficulty maintaining operations have announced their closure. The forty-odd factories that still stand firmly are reducing or stopping work due to the near-bankruptcy of the rural economy and the extreme dryness of social finance, as well as the even fiercer competition from foreign cigarettes. The business of Chinese merchants is becoming increasingly declining. Several factories have announced their closure again. Even those that are lucky enough to survive are reducing work and stopping work, making operations unstable and in a state of crisis. Compared to the booming atmosphere of the past, they cannot be mentioned in the same breath. This is why the China National Goods Cigarette Maintenance Association was organized. Since the business of Chinese factories is far from what it used to be, if they still act like swallows in a hall, content with the present and not urgently seeking salvation and a way to protect themselves, then great difficulties will arise in the future. The situation will collapse completely, and nothing will be left. Therefore, we must prepare for a rainy day and take measures to prevent problems before they arise. This is to ensure that the original business of Chinese merchants does not decline, but continues to strive towards a bright and splendid future. This is also what we, the members, are dedicated to.

Some doubt that cigarettes are a consumable item. This is true. But in general social situations, the need for cigarettes is quite extensive. All countries in the East and West are also popular. The United Kingdom and the United States are also famous tobacco-producing regions, exporting large quantities of cigarettes and tobacco leaves every year, occupying an important position in foreign trade. Therefore, governments promote and reward them to promote the development of industry. As for our country's tobacco-producing regions, there are many. Moreover, foreign cigarettes flood the market, resulting in a great outflow of wealth. Therefore, it is necessary to maintain the business of Chinese factories. Only then can the livelihoods of millions of workers be maintained, the products of tobacco farmers in various places be sold, and those who make a living from this indirectly can be without worry. Moreover, from the perspective of our country, where industry is still in its infancy, Chinese factories pay tens of millions of yuan in cigarette unified taxes every year, occupying an important position in the industry and also being a major source of income for the national treasury. Therefore, although it is a consumable item, it is crucial to the national economy and people's livelihood.

Chinese factories occupy an important position, as mentioned above. However, the heavier the position, the greater the responsibility. How should our Chinese factory colleagues conduct themselves and fulfill this important responsibility? It is important to unite with each other to consolidate the united front and move forward bravely to win the final victory. They should not each seek their own interests and only care about their own private gains, giving others a chance to take advantage and causing the disaster of being defeated individually. As for funds and talents, how should they be fully utilized? As for equipment and manufacturing, how should they be planned and improved? As for the cost of production, how should they strive to reduce it? They should all learn from the past and carefully study these issues. As for raw materials, they should especially lead by example and use domestic products as much as possible. This is to achieve the goal of mutual support and common prosperity for the entire national goods industry. If there are still domestic products that are not available and must be purchased from foreign countries, they should also work together to develop their creative spirit to solve all difficulties. This is what we deeply hope for from Chinese factories.

Alas, in this day and age, the country is in a difficult situation. The people are suffering. Just as they are waiting to recover, the tide of the global economic downturn is fiercely attacking. Our country is affected by this, and existing industries feel that they are on the verge of danger. Emerging industries are also being hit. The industries that urgently need to be maintained are not just the cigarette factory industry. Therefore, we, the members, do not dare to underestimate our own abilities and take the lead. Now, in order to expand publicity, we have designated August 8th as the National Goods Cigarette Festival and issued this special edition to loudly appeal in order to arouse the attention of our compatriots and leave a lasting impression. We sincerely hope that various industries will successively organize and support each other, so that the business of national goods will develop day by day. We also hope that the cigarette factory industry, which is growing stronger, will not be destroyed by the bad environment. This is what we cannot but hope for from the Chinese people, that they will all rise up together to maintain it.

China National Goods Cigarette Maintenance Association Standing Committee Members: Shen Xingde, Yuan Ludeng, Shen Weiting, Lao Jingxiu, Ding Houqing, Jing Yimeng, Bao Gengsheng, Ding Zhenbo, Wu Linzhi, Sun Daosheng, Shen Xuewen. Sincerely announce.

Two Optimistic Thoughts Recently 152

— Yang An

The national goods industry today has some awareness. What are they aware of? Regarding "Import Surplus" 153

— Zhu Weixuan

Since the wave of recession quickly swept across the world, it suddenly caused deep unease in various countries. Of course, our country cannot be an exception and is also affected, and society is full of recessionary sentiments!

However, the recession in foreign countries is due to increased production and oversupply, while the recession in China is due to the constraints of unequal treaties by foreign powers and the mutual pressure of natural disasters and banditry, resulting in backward industry and insufficient production. Foreigners have already seen this, so they try to import excess goods into China as much as possible, exchanging them for white silver dollars, reducing the severity of their recession. But China is getting poorer and poorer, obviously creating a country with a huge import surplus!

In fact, import surplus in international trade is also a very common phenomenon. A country with an import surplus is not necessarily harmful to its own country. As for some that are detrimental, it depends on the nature of the imported goods. If the imported goods are raw materials such as machinery and steel, then although money flows out, the result can greatly increase production and exports. Isn't this kind of import surplus a great benefit?

However, let's try to list the imported goods in China: mostly rice, sugar, oil, cloth, cosmetics, etc., all of which are purely consumable products that cannot be re-produced to pay for the imported goods. As a result, cash continues to flow out!

As for trade between foreign countries, it is based entirely on the principles of equality and reciprocity, exchanging industrial products for industrial products, exchanging what is available for what is not, and both parties benefit. China, however, not only pays in cash, but also exports mostly crude and cheap raw materials. Foreigners add packaging and sell them for multiple times the value. In the end, we are still the ones who suffer!

So, here, I think we should not calculate the import surplus and export surplus with short-sighted eyes. In order to develop industry and increase production efficiency, we should make more use of foreign production tools, such as steel, raw materials, machinery, and production equipment. Import surplus is inevitable when developing production. On the contrary, the large-scale export of raw materials is not something to be optimistic about! Compatriots! We must completely transform imported consumer goods into direct or indirect production goods. Then, even using foreign goods is equivalent to promoting national goods. In the future, industry and commerce will advance by leaps and bounds, production will increase significantly, and self-sufficiency will be achieved, and the import surplus will gradually decrease!

The National Goods Industry After the Implementation of Industrial and Commercial Loans 154

— Xuan Wan

— Should Strive for More Fundamental Solutions

After a long period of preparation and several negotiations with the government, industrial and commercial loans finally began to be implemented the day before yesterday. In the current situation where the recession is enveloping the entire market of our country, a wave of industry and commerce is dying out, and the financial community is firmly holding on to a tight policy. Now, we have unexpectedly obtained such a large sum of money as a supplement to make economic turnover flexible. I think, of course, many industries will be able to use this to overcome the crisis and create a new path for the future of national goods, giving the market a very good influence. Its effect and power cannot be ignored.

However, here I also deeply feel that this method of industrial and commercial credit lending is really only a stopgap measure. Moreover, the total amount for the entire city is only 5 million yuan, and each household is limited to 5,000 yuan. In such a large city, the gathering place of national industries, the limit is so small that it is inevitable that it will be a drop in the bucket. Therefore, during the handling of the loan, I dare to express the most ardent hope that the industrial and commercial circles and the financial circles will not forget the fundamental revival movement, that is, the national goods movement. We must know that there have been huge import surpluses over the years, and huge amounts of waste have flowed out. Under such circumstances, how can the national economy not be poor and how can industry and commerce not decline? Even according to the customs reports of the past two years, the import and export trade of our country has decreased significantly, and the amount of import surplus has also been relatively reduced, but that precisely reflects the weakness of the purchasing power of our general public, and the market is becoming increasingly bleak. If the import and export trade is estimated, the import surplus has not decreased slightly. The improvement of China's economic future and the development of national goods production and industry and commerce are always hopeless.

Therefore, in the end, I dare to point out very definitely that our current national goods industry, under the new economic assistance, must seek to consolidate its own foundation and work hard from various fundamental ideas, such as (1) resolving industry competition, uniting to save ourselves, (2) improving technology, reducing costs, and selling at the lowest price to compete with foreign goods, (4) rapidly paying attention to the promotion of border provinces and the opening of overseas markets, which are the most urgent plans now. In addition, I hope to thoroughly cooperate with the financial community to create greater industrial credit lending to promote domestic industry and the export of local goods. In this way, the two aspects of treating the symptoms and treating the root cause will advance side by side, and the current misfortune of national goods can definitely turn danger into safety.
